The usual schedule. We headed downstream today to the Trilha da Esperança, which we birded from 05h45 to 12h30, reaching perhaps 200m beyond the big leafcutter ant colony. We spent a good part of the early morning around the dry igarapé working a Zigzag Heron (actually 3 or more birds), trying to digi-scope the birds. In the afternoon we tried upstream by boat, checking out the arm of the river just above the airstrip where there was a dead pirarara attracting vultures. Then it was up to the meeting of the Madeirinha and the Roosevelt, and then to the mouth of a lagoon - a short distance upstream from there is the spot for Bamboo Antshrike, in high tangles of slender vines, but the bird wasn't home. Back at the lodge by 18h00.	HO

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS260060674	2020-09-03 10:17:42	12309	species	Kawall's Parrot	Amazona kawalli			2				Brazil	BR	Amazonas	BR-AM							Pousada Rio Roosevelt	L2802116	H	-8.4942050	-60.9621497	2014-06-07	06:50:00	obsr412230	S18811941	Stationary	P21	EBIRD_CAN	280			4	1		0	1	0		with Alan Bolten and Karen Bjorndal, Semí (local guide). Birds recorded at the barreiro (clay lick) inside the forest downstream from the Inferninho rapids on the left bank of the Roosevelt. There was still a reasonable amount of water covering the parts of the barreiro we couldn't see, and the mud was deep in some spots that we could watch. The hoped-for Tapir didn't materialize, but a big highlight was a herd of 50+ White-lipped Peccaries which arrived in mid-morning to consume clay at the lick while we watched at close range. In late morning as we were finally deciding to leave, the Crimson-bellied Parakeets finally dropped down to the ground for their fill of mud.

Birds recorded on the Campinas do Cujubim trail, my first visit to this trail, which I found to be an excellent access to the rocky campina and campinarana habitats. The trail passes through a very short stretch of campinarana before entering a rocky (sandstone) campina which is quite extensive. Worth noting that the Cujubim is said to be too shallow to navigate by August/September, which means the trail would be out of range during the lowest water season.	remarkable numbers, possibly the most I've ever seen of the species at a single site in a morning. Count is exact, but undoubtedly undercounted as some groups may have passed overhead without vocalizing while we looked at other things. Birds were flying out of an area of taller campinarana in the direction of the Cujubim (which they passed over), perhaps en route to the Roosevelt to feed. Consisted of pairs and groups of 4 - 6 birds.

Birds recorded on transect #2 of the Tabajara survey/inventory project, a 5km picada through campina and campinarana. Weather quite hot and sunny. We mostly just walked straight through the campina (very dense ground cover for the first 800m or so) en route to the campinarana where we planned to look for Poecilotriccus senex (success!). Excellent trail through varzea forest (with a relatively short stretch with some thick mud) and then into higher terra firme forest with open understorey and many large emergents. We walked as far as the first forest stream in the terra firme (the first steep downward slope) before turning back. The picada runs another 3-4 km straight into the terra firme from the point where we turned back, so there is loads of potential. Bruno said he has seen many antswarms along this trail, including with Skutchia, along with other interesting species such as Red-and-black Grosbeak, Rusty-belted Tapaculo, Banded Antbird, etc.
